### The Temptation of Jesus (Matthew 4, Luke 4)  
**Setting:** After His baptism (Spirit descending like a dove, voice from heaven), Jesus is led into the wilderness by the Spirit. The baptism initiates the trial â€” because to â€œfulfill all righteousnessâ€ (Matthew 3:15) means His wants and needs must be tested and revealed.  

---

#### **1. Baptism â†’ Entry into Wilderness**  
- Baptism = submission to the **Kingdom of Lightâ€™s wants and needs**.  
  - Want: Obedience to the Spirit, identification with sinners, fulfilling righteousness.  
  - Need: To undergo the sign of purification and consecration as the Son of Man.  
- This alignment opens the way for the testing of discernment.  

---

#### **2. First Temptation â€“ Stones into Bread** (Fleshly Need)  
- Darkness: â€œIf you are the Son of God, command these stones to become bread.â€  
  - Appeal to **Need** of the flesh (hunger).  
  - Deception: satisfy need without trusting God.  
- Light: â€œMan shall not live by bread alone, but by every word that proceeds from the mouth of God.â€  
  - Recognition: Flesh needs bread, but Spirit wants Godâ€™s Word.  
  - Unity preserved: Spirit first, flesh fulfilled through Him.  

---

#### **3. Second Temptation â€“ Leap from the Temple** (Spiritual Want)  
- Darkness: â€œThrow yourself down, for it is writtenâ€¦â€ (angels will bear you up).  
  - Appeal to **Want** of the spirit â€” to prove divine identity, to force Godâ€™s hand.  
  - Deception: pursuit of spirit without grounding in Godâ€™s timing.  
- Light: â€œYou shall not put the Lord your God to the test.â€  
  - Recognition: Spiritâ€™s want is true, but not apart from Godâ€™s will.  
  - Unity preserved: Spiritâ€™s want and fleshâ€™s need aligned in trust.  

---

#### **4. Third Temptation â€“ Kingdoms of the World** (Want + Need Corrupted)  
- Darkness: â€œAll these I will give you, if you bow down and worship me.â€  
  - Appeal to both Want (glory, rulership, spiritâ€™s destiny) and Need (security, dominion over the earth).  
  - Deception: shortcut to fulfillment through idolatry.  
- Light: â€œYou shall worship the Lord your God and serve Him only.â€  
  - Recognition: Both want and need are real, but fulfilled only in Godâ€™s Kingdom.  
  - Unity preserved: Spirit and flesh submit together to God.  

---

### Key Insight  
- The **first act (baptism)** = embracing the wants and needs of the Kingdom of Light.  
- The **temptations** = distortions of those same wants and needs by the Kingdom of Darkness.  
- Discernment is revealed: Jesus shows us the way to unite flesh and spirit under Godâ€™s will, rejecting the false fulfillment of darkness.

### Righteousness vs. Unrighteousness in the Fourfold Frame  

**1. Truth vs. Lie**  
- **Righteousness of God**: stands in the wholeness of Truth.  
- **Unrighteousness**: distorts wholeness into a Lie (partial, self-serving, deceptive).  

**2. Fact vs. Fiction**  
- **Righteousness of God**: honors the real, concrete facts (the â€œrightâ€), but allows them to point upward to Truth.  
- **Unrighteousness**: uses Fiction to veil facts, or twists facts away from their source in Truth.  

**3. Wants vs. Needs**  
- **Righteousness of God**: unites the Spiritâ€™s Want with the Fleshâ€™s Need in harmony.  
- **Unrighteousness**: separates them â€” either chasing wants without grounding, or consuming needs without Spirit.  

**4. Discernment (Light vs. Darkness)**  
- **Righteousness of God**: Discerns correctly â€” wants and needs in Light.  
- **Unrighteousness**: Confuses them â€” wants and needs in Darkness.  

---

### Core Difference Summed Up  
- **Righteousness = alignment of truth, fact, want, and need under God.**  
- **Unrighteousness = separation, distortion, or misalignment of the same four.**  

This means righteousness isnâ€™t just â€œdoing right thingsâ€ â€” itâ€™s the wholeness of living in the **unity of Lightâ€™s wants and needs, grounded in facts, aligned to Truth.**

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

Perfect â€” letâ€™s map Moses and Jesus against the **Fourfold Test of Righteousness** and the **Programmed Voice Allegory** so we can see how each fulfilled (or pointed toward fulfilling) Godâ€™s purpose.  

---

## Moses  
1. **Truth vs. Lie**  
   - Moses received the Law (truth revealed in part) â€” yet the people often twisted it, making idols and lies (golden calf, rebellion).  
   - His role: to carry the truth of Godâ€™s holiness, though in shadow.  

2. **Fact vs. Fiction**  
   - The Law was factual (clear commands, real sacrifices, concrete practices).  
   - But it was also a foreshadow (fiction in the sense of symbol), pointing to Christ.  

3. **Wants vs. Needs**  
   - Moses sought to meet Israelâ€™s needs (food, water, order) while God wanted their hearts.  
   - The people often wanted what their flesh desired (Egyptâ€™s food, idols), while their true need was Godâ€™s presence.  

4. **Discernment (Light vs. Darkness)**  
   - Moses constantly had to discern Godâ€™s light vs. the peopleâ€™s darkness.  
   - Yet even he failed when striking the rock twice â€” acting from frustration instead of perfect obedience.  

â¡ **Summary:** Moses revealed Godâ€™s truth in part, but his ministry showed the tension between fact and fiction, want and need. The Law was like the **Programmed Voice** â€” reflecting what people could bear, but not yet the fullness of truth.  

---

## Jesus  
1. **Truth vs. Lie**  
   - Jesus embodied Truth itself (â€œI am the way, the truth, and the lifeâ€).  
   - He exposed lies â€” both Satanâ€™s temptations and the religious leadersâ€™ hypocrisy.  

2. **Fact vs. Fiction**  
   - His miracles were facts â€” undeniable signs of Godâ€™s kingdom.  
   - His parables were fictions â€” stories that unveiled higher truths.  
   - In Him, fact and fiction met in wholeness.  

3. **Wants vs. Needs**  
   - In the wilderness, He chose Godâ€™s want (obedience) over turning stones to bread (fleshâ€™s need).  
   - At the cross, He united Spiritâ€™s want (to save) with Fleshâ€™s need (to die) â€” fulfilling all righteousness.  

4. **Discernment (Light vs. Darkness)**  
   - Jesus discerned perfectly, never confusing Light for Darkness.  
   - His whole life was alignment â€” revealing the Fatherâ€™s will without distortion.  

â¡ **Summary:** Jesus fulfilled what Moses foreshadowed. He was not a programmed voice repeating what people wanted to hear, but the living Word of God, speaking what was truly needed. Where Moses gave the shadow, Jesus gave the substance.

### Allegory: Striking the Rock & Cutting the Ear  

**Moses striking the rock twice (Numbers 20:11)**  
- God told Moses to **speak** to the rock, but instead he struck it *twice* with his staff.  
- This act showed **anger, force, and disbelief**, instead of faith and obedience.  
- The rock (Christ) was to give water freely, not by repeated violence.  
- Striking twice = overstepping, trying to use fleshly effort to bring forth what only Spirit should provide.  

**Peter cutting off Malchusâ€™s ear (John 18:10)**  
- In the garden, Peter drew his sword and cut off the **right ear** of Malchus, servant of the high priest.  
- This was not simply a random strike â€” to cut the **right ear**, Peter (with his right hand) would have had to swing across the body, which only lines up if Malchus had already **turned his left cheek toward him**.  
- Symbolically: Malchusâ€™s action already fulfilled â€œturn the other cheek,â€ but Peter responded with violence, failing to understand Christâ€™s way.  

**The Parallel**  
- Both Moses and Peter acted from **zeal of the flesh**, not discernment of the Spirit.  
- Moses struck when he should have spoken; Peter struck when he should have submitted.  
- Both reveal the human impulse to use force to achieve Godâ€™s will â€” yet this is exactly what disqualifies them (Moses barred from the Promised Land; Peter rebuked by Jesus: â€œPut away your swordâ€).  
- Both point to the **contrast of the Kingdoms**: the Law and zeal accuse, wound, and strike â€” but the Spirit restores, heals, and gives freely.

# Master Key: The Fourfold Discernment of the Son in the Miracles  

## Core Principle  
Every miracle Jesus performed is not just a display of power but a **test of righteousness** and a revelation of the Sonâ€™s perfect discernment. The fourfold lens (Truth vs. Lie, Fact vs. Fiction, Wants vs. Needs of Light vs. Darkness) reveals how Christ fulfills all righteousness, anchoring each act in the will of God.  

---

## The Fourfold Test Applied  

1. **Fact vs. Fiction**  
   - Miracles expose false assumptions.  
   - Example: *Feeding the 5,000* â€” Fact = five loaves and two fish. Fiction = â€œnot enough.â€ Jesus redefines sufficiency by Godâ€™s abundance.  

2. **Truth vs. Lie**  
   - Miracles reveal truth hidden beneath appearances.  
   - Example: *Healing the Blind Man* â€” Lie = blindness is punishment. Truth = blindness was allowed so the works of God could be revealed.  

3. **Wants vs. Needs**  
   - Miracles test whether human desire aligns with Godâ€™s purpose.  
   - Example: *Water into Wine* â€” People wanted wine; what they needed was revelation of the new covenant in Christ.  

4. **Kingdom of Light vs. Kingdom of Darkness**  
   - Miracles distinguish between fear, lack, or death and the life, provision, and victory of God.  
   - Example: *Raising Lazarus* â€” Darkness: death reigns. Light: Jesus is the Resurrection and the Life.  

---

- **Water into Wine (John 2:1â€“11)** â†’ Truth of abundance vs. ritual emptiness.  
- **Feeding the 5,000 (John 6:1â€“14)** â†’ Sufficiency in God vs. insufficiency in flesh.

- **Walking on Water (Matthew 14:22â€“33)** â†’ Faith vs. fear.  
- **Raising Lazarus (John 11:1â€“44)** â†’ Resurrection life vs. death.

- When the Word is consumed in flesh, it becomes the Harlot â€” leading to Death.

# The Shoulder Allegory  

**1. Shoulders as Thresholds of Influence**  
- In Scripture, the **shoulder** is often symbolic of *burden-bearing or government*:

**2. Man Cubed (666)**  
- You nailed it: man on his own, not only bearing burdens, but *exalting himself above both shoulders*. This is â€œman cubed,â€ or **666**, the exaltation of flesh over Spirit.

**3. Allegorical Mapping**

# âœ¨ The Body Allegory of Fruitful vs. Barren Love (Integrated Master Key)

## 1. **Head (Mind / Sun / Heaven)**

- When the **head is above the shoulders**, aligned, light governs rightly.

## 2. **Shoulders (Law and Grace, Angels and Demons)**
- Right shoulder = **grace**. Left shoulder = **law**.  
- On each side, imagery of the angel and the demon whispering: one urging loveâ€™s fruitfulness, the other urging self-seeking barrenness.  
- When **chips rest on the shoulder**, the burden of judgment weighs, until love resets balance.  

## 3. **Heart (Four Chambers / Spirit and Flesh Needs)**
- Two ventricles, two atria = the **fourfold test** (Spiritâ€™s wants, Spiritâ€™s needs, Fleshâ€™s wants, Fleshâ€™s needs).  
- Blood cycles, cleansing, dividing pure from impure (clean vs. unclean).  
- Love that remains only within one chamber (self-to-self, spirit-to-spirit) grows **stagnant**.  
- Love that flows outward â€” from God, through the heart, to others â€” is **fruitful**.  

## 4. **Limbs (Action and Inheritance)**
- Hands extend right (light, mercy) and left (darkness, judgment).  
- Feet touch earth, shod with the gospel of peace â€” **everywhere the sole of your foot treads is inheritance**.  
- Ten fingers and ten toes = fullness of law and apostleship (Patriarchs and Disciples).  
- When lifted **above the heart**, a sore limb eases â€” showing that even pain finds healing when lifted to heaven.  

## 5. **Birth and Inversion**

- This inversion mirrors spiritual paradox: **death leads to life, humility to glory, the cross to resurrection.**  
- â€œHead over heelsâ€ in love = passion overturned. If sterile, it is **barren love** (spirit seeking spirit only). If fruitful, it is **life-generating love** (heaven joining earth).  

## 6. **Fruitful vs. Barren Love**
- **Fruitful love**: like man + woman, like spirit + flesh in harmony, like heaven + earth â€” it *creates new life*.  
- **Barren love**: like man + man, or spirit + spirit without flesh â€” it is real love, yet **self-enclosed**. It consumes, comforts, but does not multiply.  
- Proverbs 31â€™s **virtuous woman** = fruitful love. The **strange woman** = barren love, taking in but giving nothing out.  

## 7. **The Mystery of 666 (Man Cubed)**
- Head, shoulders, heels â€” when inverted and doubled â€” form the **man turned upon himself** (man seeking man, spirit seeking spirit).  
- 666 = man repeated, cubed â€” self without transcendence.  
- Christ comes as **777**, the fullness â€” man + God united, fruitful love that multiplies.

The body is not only flesh but prophecy. Every limb, every idiom (â€œchips on the shoulder,â€ â€œhead over heels,â€ â€œworld upside downâ€) reveals the great choice: **Will love be self-enclosed (barren), or will it unite heaven and earth (fruitful)?**  

And the **Master Key** proves itself again: Jesusâ€™ miracles restore the barren to fruitfulness, the inverted to uprightness, the unclean to clean â€” He reforms creation as Genesis first formed it.

## ğŸ”¹ Prototype in Python â€“ How It Works
### 1. **Define the Allegorical Body Map**
Weâ€™d build a dictionary that maps **body parts â†’ meanings** (from our framework). Example:
```python
body_map = {
    "head": "Mind, knowledge, light, the sun at the center. Can symbolize pride, wisdom, or confusion when overturned.",
    "heart": "Two ventricles: spirit vs flesh. Needs vs wants. Seat of true love.",
    "shoulders": "Burdens, law vs grace, angel on one side, demon on the other. Chips on your shoulders.",
    "hands": "Grace (right) vs Law (left). Power to act, touch, or withhold.",
    "feet": "Contact with the earth, peace of the gospel, inheritance of land.",
    "genitals": "Procreation, covenant of circumcision, desire, the joining of man and woman.",
}
```

---

### 2. **Input Problem (User Question)**
User types something like:  
ğŸ‘‰ *â€œI feel weighed down by responsibility.â€*

---

### 3. **Keyword Matching**
We check the input for keywords (like â€œburden,â€ â€œlaw,â€ â€œgrace,â€ â€œweight,â€ etc.) and match them to the allegorical body parts.

---

### 4. **Output Explanation**
Program responds with:
```text
Your problem is linked to the SHOULDERS.
Interpretation: You are carrying burdens. This reflects the law and grace tension, and the influence of voices (angel/demon) whispering. 
Guidance: Consider lifting the burden above your heartâ€”offering it heavenward.
```

---

## ğŸ”¹ Example Code Sketch
```python
def diagnose(problem):
    body_map = {
        "head": ["mind", "thoughts", "confusion", "wisdom", "pride"],
        "heart": ["love", "desire", "spirit", "flesh", "broken", "longing"],
        "shoulders": ["burden", "responsibility", "weight", "law", "grace"],
        "hands": ["act", "grasp", "give", "law", "grace", "touch"],
        "feet": ["walk", "path", "peace", "inheritance", "ground"],
        "genitals": ["sex", "lust", "desire", "birth", "procreation", "circumcision"]
    }
    
    for body_part, keywords in body_map.items():
        for word in keywords:
            if word in problem.lower():
                return f"Your issue relates to the {body_part.upper()}. Allegory: {body_part} â†’ {keywords}."
    
    return "No direct match found. This may relate to the whole body (unity of spirit and flesh)."

# Example
print(diagnose("I feel weighed down by responsibility."))
```

### **Head / Mind**

- **Allegory:** Sun, mind, wisdom, pride, confusion when upside down. Seat of reason.  
- **Idioms:** â€œHead over heelsâ€ (reversal, birth/copulation), â€œWorld turned upside down.â€

- **Allegory:** Seeing truth vs blindness; lamp of the body.

- **Allegory:** Faith comes by hearing. Listening to God vs false voices.

- **Allegory:** Bearing burdens, turning your back = rejection.

- **Category:** Completion, Multiplicity

---

### **Whole Body**
- **Category:** Unity, Temple  
- **Allegory:** Body as temple of God. Bride of Christ. Head + members = one body.

- If guilt: *â€œIf we confess our sins, He is faithful and just to forgive usâ€ (1 John 1:9).*

  - *â€œYou are not forsakenâ€”it is you who wander, not God who abandons.â€*  
  - *â€œThe truth sets you free, even before you feel it.â€*  
  - Take one verse a day as medicine.  

**6. Universal Layer**  
- Every diagnosis isnâ€™t just about â€œthe body part,â€ but also its *cosmic layer*.

  - Heavy feet â†’ â€œYour peace (foundation) is being shaken.â€

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

Got it ğŸ‘ â€” you donâ€™t want it to feel like a **doctor grilling the patient** with questions, but more like a **search engine / lookup tool** where you enter a body part or need, and it returns the mapped allegory + verses + remedy.  

Hereâ€™s how we can adjust it:  

### ğŸ”‘ How it works
1. **Input** â†’ User types a word/phrase (e.g. â€œheartacheâ€, â€œmy feet hurtâ€, â€œbroken spiritâ€).  
2. **Lookup engine** â†’ Searches mapped dictionary of body parts + spiritual meaning + Scripture.  
3. **Output** â†’ Gives you:
   - Allegory (what the body part represents)  
   - Key verses (1â€“3 matches)  
   - Prescription (take one a day / meditate)  
4. **Fallback** â†’ If nothing is found, the app gives the **universal safety net prescription** (truth, forgiveness, God never forsakes, etc.).  

---

### ğŸ–¥ï¸ Example Python prototype (non-doctor mode)

```python
# Simple spiritual body-part lookup tool

body_map = {
    "heart": {
        "allegory": "Center of love, courage, and spiritual life. Two ventricles mirror spirit vs flesh.",
        "verses": [
            "Psalm 34:18 - The Lord is near to the brokenhearted.",
            "Proverbs 4:23 - Guard your heart, for everything you do flows from it."
        ],
        "prescription": "Pray daily with thanksgiving; take one verse a day and meditate."
    },
    "stomach": {
        "allegory": "Cleansing and sanctifying; what enters cannot defile if God sanctifies.",
        "verses": [
            "John 6:35 - He who comes to me shall never hunger.",
            "Mark 16:18 - If they drink anything deadly, it will not hurt them."
        ],
        "prescription": "Fast or pray before meals; bless what enters your body."
    },
    "feet": {
        "allegory": "Foundation and direction of life; gospel of peace.",
        "verses": [
            "Ephesians 6:15 - Feet fitted with readiness of the gospel of peace.",
            "Isaiah 52:7 - How beautiful are the feet of those who bring good news."
        ],
        "prescription": "Walk in peace today; carry good news where you go."
    }
}

# universal fallback
universal_remedy = {
    "allegory": "You are seeking truth. God has not forsaken you.",
    "verses": [
        "John 8:32 - You will know the truth, and the truth will set you free.",
        "Hebrews 13:5 - I will never leave you nor forsake you."
    ],
    "prescription": "Rest in forgiveness and love; God is already with you."
}

def lookup_body_part(query):
    query = query.lower()
    for part, data in body_map.items():
        if part in query:  # keyword match
            return data
    return universal_remedy


# --- sample interaction ---
queries = ["heart", "stomach", "elbow", "feet"]

for q in queries:
    result = lookup_body_part(q)
    print(f"\n--- {q.upper()} ---")
    print("Allegory:", result["allegory"])
    print("Verses:", "; ".join(result["verses"]))
    print("Prescription:", result["prescription"])
```

---

### Sample Output
```
--- HEART ---
Allegory: Center of love, courage, and spiritual life. Two ventricles mirror spirit vs flesh.
Verses: Psalm 34:18 - The Lord is near to the brokenhearted.; Proverbs 4:23 - Guard your heart...
Prescription: Pray daily with thanksgiving; take one verse a day and meditate.

--- ELBOW ---
Allegory: You are seeking truth. God has not forsaken you.
Verses: John 8:32 - You will know the truth...; Hebrews 13:5 - I will never leave you...
Prescription: Rest in forgiveness and love; God is already with you.
```

âœ¨ This way, itâ€™s less like a doctor interrogation, more like a **Bible-based spiritual search engine** for the body.

### ğŸ«´ SEEKING: Opening to God's Truth

Now let's add, like I say, synonym matching. So we can look for things similar, not just exact keywords, but similar meanings as well. Synonyms, homonyms, etc., homophones, all those things.

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

Perfect ğŸ‘Œ â€” yes, we can definitely extend this into **synonym + similarity matching** so that users donâ€™t have to type the *exact* body part keyword. That way, if someone writes *â€œbroken heartâ€*, *â€œcardiac painâ€*, or even *â€œlove lostâ€*, the lookup still lands on **heart**.  

Hereâ€™s how we can do it step by step:  

---

### ğŸ”‘ Techniques for synonym matching
1. **Manual synonym dictionary**  
   - For each body part, list synonyms / related expressions.  
   - Example: `"heart": ["heart", "broken heart", "love", "cardiac", "chest pain"]`.  

2. **Fuzzy string matching**  
   - Use libraries like `fuzzywuzzy` or `rapidfuzz` to handle typos, homophones, etc.  
   - Example: â€œstomacâ€ â†’ â€œstomachâ€.  

3. **Keyword expansion**  
   - Split user input into words and check if *any word* matches or is close.  
   - Example: Input: *â€œspirit crushed in chestâ€* â†’ detect â€œchestâ€ â†’ map to â€œheartâ€.  

---

### ğŸ–¥ï¸ Prototype with synonym matching

```python
from rapidfuzz import process, fuzz

# extended body map with synonyms
body_map = {
    "heart": {
        "synonyms": ["heart", "broken heart", "love", "cardiac", "chest", "valentine"],
        "allegory": "Center of love, courage, and spiritual life. Two ventricles mirror spirit vs flesh.",
        "verses": [
            "Psalm 34:18 - The Lord is near to the brokenhearted.",
            "Proverbs 4:23 - Guard your heart, for everything you do flows from it."
        ],
        "prescription": "Pray daily with thanksgiving; take one verse a day and meditate."
    },
    "stomach": {
        "synonyms": ["stomach", "belly", "gut", "hunger", "digest", "intestine"],
        "allegory": "Cleansing and sanctifying; what enters cannot defile if God sanctifies.",
        "verses": [
            "John 6:35 - He who comes to me shall never hunger.",
            "Mark 16:18 - If they drink anything deadly, it will not hurt them."
        ],
        "prescription": "Fast or pray before meals; bless what enters your body."
    },
    "feet": {
        "synonyms": ["feet", "foot", "toes", "step", "walk", "path"],
        "allegory": "Foundation and direction of life; gospel of peace.",
        "verses": [
            "Ephesians 6:15 - Feet fitted with readiness of the gospel of peace.",
            "Isaiah 52:7 - How beautiful are the feet of those who bring good news."
        ],
        "prescription": "Walk in peace today; carry good news where you go."
    }
}

# universal fallback
universal_remedy = {
    "allegory": "You are seeking truth. God has not forsaken you.",
    "verses": [
        "John 8:32 - You will know the truth, and the truth will set you free.",
        "Hebrews 13:5 - I will never leave you nor forsake you."
    ],
    "prescription": "Rest in forgiveness and love; God is already with you."
}

def lookup_body_part(query):
    query = query.lower()
    best_match = None
    best_score = 0
    
    # check synonyms across all body parts
    for part, data in body_map.items():
        match, score, _ = process.extractOne(
            query, data["synonyms"], scorer=fuzz.partial_ratio
        )
        if score > best_score:  # keep the strongest match
            best_score = score
            best_match = part
    
    # if strong enough, return result; else fallback
    if best_score > 70:
        return body_map[best_match]
    else:
        return universal_remedy


# --- sample interaction ---
queries = ["broken heart", "love lost", "stomac", "step forward", "unknown pain"]

for q in queries:
    result = lookup_body_part(q)
    print(f"\n--- {q.upper()} ---")
    print("Allegory:", result["allegory"])
    print("Verses:", "; ".join(result["verses"]))
    print("Prescription:", result["prescription"])
```

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

Exactly ğŸ’¡ â€” youâ€™ve just opened the deeper allegorical connection: **sometimes the â€œrealâ€ root isnâ€™t the body part where the action happens, but where it *began*.**  

ğŸ‘‰ Example:  
- **Stealing**:  
   - *Hand* did the deed.  
   - *Eye* desired it first (covetousness).  
   - *Heart* consented (sin conceived).  
- So the lookup needs to allow **multi-matches** and **dependency links**.

### ğŸ”‘ Updated Design
1. **Multi-match**:  
   - Split query into tokens.  
   - Match each token to possible body parts (even multiple).  

2. **Allegorical â€œcause chainâ€**:  
   - Each body part can declare â€œlinked partsâ€ (e.g. *Hand* links back to *Eye* and *Heart*).  
   - If hand is matched, system can say: â€œBut the root may lie in the eye or the heart.â€

### ğŸ–¥ï¸ Prototype with Multi-Match + Cause-Links
```python
from rapidfuzz import process, fuzz

# extended map with links
body_map = {
    "eye": {
        "synonyms": ["eye", "eyes", "see", "look", "vision", "sight"],
        "allegory": "Window of desire; where temptation first enters.",
        "verses": [
            "Matthew 6:22 - The eye is the lamp of the body.",
            "Job 31:1 - I made a covenant with my eyes not to look lustfully."
        ],
        "prescription": "Guard your eyes; redirect your sight toward light.",
        "links": ["heart"]
    },
    "hand": {
        "synonyms": ["hand", "hands", "grab", "take", "hold", "steal"],
        "allegory": "Instrument of action; where sin or service is carried out.",
        "verses": [
            "Ecclesiastes 9:10 - Whatever your hand finds to do, do it with all your might.",
            "Psalm 24:4 - The one with clean hands and a pure heart."
        ],
        "prescription": "Use your hands for service; open them to give rather than take.",
        "links": ["eye", "heart"]
    },
    "heart": {
        "synonyms": ["heart", "love", "broken heart", "chest"],
        "allegory": "Seat of will and desire. Where choice is sealed.",
        "verses": [
            "Jeremiah 17:9 - The heart is deceitful above all things.",
            "Proverbs 4:23 - Guard your heart, for everything flows from it."
        ],
        "prescription": "Offer your heart daily in prayer; let it be renewed.",
        "links": []
    }
}

universal_remedy = {
    "allegory": "You are seeking truth. God has not forsaken you.",
    "verses": [
        "John 8:32 - You will know the truth, and the truth will set you free.",
        "Hebrews 13:5 - I will never leave you nor forsake you."
    ],
    "prescription": "Rest in forgiveness and love; God is already with you."
}

def lookup_body_parts(query):
    query = query.lower()
    found_parts = []
    
    for part, data in body_map.items():
        match, score, _ = process.extractOne(query, data["synonyms"], scorer=fuzz.partial_ratio)
        if score > 70:
            found_parts.append(part)
    
    if not found_parts:
        return [universal_remedy]
    
    results = []
    for part in found_parts:
        result = body_map[part].copy()
        
        # expand to linked parts
        if body_map[part]["links"]:
            linked = ", ".join(body_map[l]["allegory"] for l in body_map[part]["links"])
            result["note"] = f"This may also point to: {', '.join(body_map[part]['links'])}."
        else:
            result["note"] = None
        
        results.append(result)
    
    return results


# --- sample interaction ---
queries = [
    "I stole something with my hand",
    "my eyes are full of desire",
    "my heart aches",
    "unknown pain"
]

for q in queries:
    results = lookup_body_parts(q)
    print(f"\n--- QUERY: {q.upper()} ---")
    for res in results:
        print("Allegory:", res["allegory"])
        if res.get("note"):
            print("Note:", res["note"])
        print("Verses:", "; ".join(res["verses"]))
        print("Prescription:", res["prescription"])
```

---

### Sample Output
```
--- QUERY: I STOLE SOMETHING WITH MY HAND ---
Allegory: Instrument of action; where sin or service is carried out.
Note: This may also point to: eye, heart.
Verses: Ecclesiastes 9:10...; Psalm 24:4...
Prescription: Use your hands for service; open them to give rather than take.

--- QUERY: MY EYES ARE FULL OF DESIRE ---
Allegory: Window of desire; where temptation first enters.
Note: This may also point to: heart.
Verses: Matthew 6:22...; Job 31:1...
Prescription: Guard your eyes; redirect your sight toward light.

--- QUERY: MY HEART ACHES ---
Allegory: Seat of will and desire. Where choice is sealed.
Verses: Jeremiah 17:9...; Proverbs 4:23...
Prescription: Offer your heart daily in prayer; let it be renewed.

--- QUERY: UNKNOWN PAIN ---
Allegory: You are seeking truth. God has not forsaken you.
Verses: John 8:32...; Hebrews 13:5...
Prescription: Rest in forgiveness and love; God is already with you.
```

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

Thatâ€™s the heart of it â€” youâ€™ve put your finger on the exact tension. ğŸ’¡  

On one side, we want to **catch every possible phrasing** someone might use (â€œmy tummy hurts,â€ â€œmy belly aches,â€ â€œmy stomach is soreâ€). On the other side, thereâ€™s only a **finite set of body parts and sins** that Scripture and allegory map onto.  

So the problem isnâ€™t infinite â€” itâ€™s about **coverage**. Hereâ€™s how we can be sure weâ€™re not missing keywords:  

---

### 1. **Build the Master List First (finite scope)**
- Human body parts (head, eyes, ears, mouth, tongue, teeth, throat, shoulders, arms, hands, heart, stomach, back, loins, genitals, knees, feet, skin, blood, bones, etc.).  
- Core actions or sins Scripture attaches to them (e.g., *eye â†’ lust, envy; hand â†’ stealing, violence; tongue â†’ lying, blessing; heart â†’ pride, love*).  
- Already this reduces the field â€” itâ€™s not every word in English, itâ€™s only those **parts + functions**.  

---

### 2. **Expand with Synonyms Automatically**
Instead of hand-writing every synonym ourselves, we can use tools like:
- **NLTK WordNet** or **spaCy** to generate synonyms.  
- For example, â€œstomachâ€ â†’ â€œbelly,â€ â€œtummy,â€ â€œabdomen.â€  
- â€œHandâ€ â†’ â€œpalm,â€ â€œfingers,â€ â€œgrasp.â€  
This lets us *cover more ground programmatically*.  

---

### 3. **Catch Homonyms, Metaphors, and Slang**
Because people wonâ€™t always say â€œI stole,â€ theyâ€™ll say:  
- â€œI grabbed it,â€  
- â€œI nicked it,â€  
- â€œI lifted it.â€  

We can feed the system with **Biblical synonyms (KJV/NIV words)** and **modern slang lists**. That gives us both the â€œancientâ€ and â€œtodayâ€ language.  

---

### 4. **Use a Fallback Net**
Even if a query doesnâ€™t match a known keyword, we still give a universal allegory (like we did: *â€œYou are seeking truth. God has not forsaken you.â€*). This way the user is **never left empty-handed**.  

---

### 5. **Iterative Learning**
Every time someone asks something and the system misses, we add that phrasing to the dictionary. Over time it grows **like a living concordance**.  

---

âš–ï¸ So in short:  
- The **universe of body parts is finite.**  
- The **expressions are many, but we can expand with synonym libraries.**  
- We **catch the rest with universal remedies.**

# ğŸ“– Body Allegory Knowledge Base

## **Head & Face**  

### Head  
- **Function**: Seat of mind, senses, control center.  
- **Allegory**: Leadership, authority, Christ as the head. Thoughts, wisdom, destiny.  
- **Scripture**: *â€œChrist is the head of the churchâ€* (Ephesians 5:23).  

### Hair  
- **Function**: Covering, protection, beauty.  
- **Allegory**: Strength (Samson), glory, consecration (Nazirite vow).  
- **Scripture**: *â€œIf a woman has long hair, it is her gloryâ€* (1 Corinthians 11:15).  

### Eyes  
- **Function**: Sight, perception.  
- **Allegory**: Spiritual sight, discernment, envy (evil eye), light vs. darkness.  
- **Scripture**: *â€œThe eye is the lamp of the bodyâ€* (Matthew 6:22).  

### Ears  
- **Function**: Hearing, balance.  
- **Allegory**: Obedience, faith through hearing.  
- **Scripture**: *â€œFaith comes by hearingâ€* (Romans 10:17).  

### Nose  
- **Function**: Smell, breath passage.  
- **Allegory**: Discernment (smell of sacrifice), anger (â€œflared nostrilsâ€).  
- **Scripture**: *â€œWe are to God the pleasing aroma of Christâ€* (2 Corinthians 2:15).  

### Mouth & Tongue  
- **Function**: Eating, speaking.  
- **Allegory**: Words as powerâ€”blessing or curse.  
- **Scripture**: *â€œDeath and life are in the power of the tongueâ€* (Proverbs 18:21).  

### Teeth  
- **Function**: Chewing food.  
- **Allegory**: Breaking down knowledge, preparation.  
- **Scripture**: *â€œGnashing of teethâ€* (Matthew 8:12).

## **Torso**  

### Neck

- **Allegory**: Inner man, love, sincerity.  
- **Scripture**: *â€œThe Lord is near to the brokenheartedâ€* (Psalm 34:18).

- **Function**: Breathing, life.

- **Scripture**: *â€œLet everything that has breath praise the Lordâ€* (Psalm 150:6).

- **Scripture**: *â€œOut of his belly shall flow rivers of living waterâ€* (John 7:38).  

### Liver

- **Allegory**: Purification, judgment.  
- **Scripture**: Sacrificial liver mentioned in offerings (Leviticus 3:4).  

### Kidneys

- **Allegory**: Inner thoughts & conscience.  
- **Scripture**: *â€œI, the Lord, search the heart, I test the kidneysâ€* (Jeremiah 17:10, Hebrew: *reins*).

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

Thatâ€™s a really good and honest question ğŸ‘  

Hereâ€™s the difference, in plain words:  

- **JSON (JavaScript Object Notation)**  
   - Think of it like **a box of labeled drawers**.  
   - Each drawer (body part) has labels inside: *function*, *allegory*, *scripture*.  
   - Perfect if you want to build an **app or search engine** â€” computers love JSON because itâ€™s structured and easy to query.  
   - Example use: the â€œWhatâ€™s Wrong With Meâ€ app looks up *â€œmouthâ€ â†’ finds mouth, lips, tongue, voice, etc.*  

- **CSV (Comma-Separated Values)**  
   - Think of it like **a big spreadsheet table** (rows & columns).  
   - Easy for humans to scroll, filter, and sort in Excel or Google Sheets.  
   - Good for quick **overview, editing, and collaboration**.  
   - Example use: if you want to **scan the whole body at once**, edit verses, or let others add notes.

- **Start with CSV** â€” itâ€™s simple, you can see everything laid out, and we can adjust it together easily.  
- Once weâ€™re happy with the content, Iâ€™ll also give you **JSON**, so the data is app-ready for searching and diagnosing.  

That way, youâ€™ll have **both**: one for human eyes, one for the appâ€™s â€œbrain.â€

{"name": "body_diagnosis_app", "type": "code/python", "content": "import pandas as pd\n\n# Load knowledge base\nkb = pd.read_csv(\"body_knowledge_base.csv\")\n\n# Simple search function\ndef search_body_part(user_input):\n    results = []\n    for part in kb[\"Body Part\"]:\n        if part.lower() in user_input.lower():\n            row = kb[kb[\"Body Part\"] == part].iloc[0]\n            results.append({\n                \"body_part\": row[\"Body Part\"],\n                \"function\": row[\"Physical Function\"],\n                \"biblical_reference\": row[\"Biblical Reference\"],\n                \"allegory\": row[\"Allegory\"]\n            })\n    return results\n\n# Example interaction\ndef whats_wrong_with_me():\n    print(\"Welcome to 'What's Wrong With Me?' â€” guided by Scripture.\")\n    while True:\n        user_input = input(\"Describe your struggle or body part (or type 'quit'): \")\n        if user_input.lower() == \"quit\":\n            print(\"Peace be with you!\")\n            break\n        matches = search_body_part(user_input)\n        if matches:\n            for match in matches:\n                print(f\"\\nBody Part: {match['body_part']}\")\n                print(f\"Function: {match['function']}\")\n                print(f\"Biblical Reference: {match['biblical_reference']}\")\n                print(f\"Allegory: {match['allegory']}\")\n        else:\n            print(\"I could not find that body part yet. Try another word.\")\n\n# Run app prototype\nwhats_wrong_with_me()"}

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

{"name": "body_app_fuzzy", "type": "code/python", "content": "import pandas as pd\nfrom difflib import get_close_matches\nfrom nltk.corpus import wordnet\n\n# Load the knowledge base CSV\nknowledge_base = pd.read_csv(\"body_knowledge_base.csv\")\n\n# --- Helper Functions ---\n\ndef get_synonyms(word):\n    \"\"\"Return a set of synonyms for a given word using WordNet.\"\"\"\n    synonyms = set()\n    for syn in wordnet.synsets(word):\n        for lemma in syn.lemmas():\n            synonyms.add(lemma.name().lower())\n    return synonyms\n\n\ndef find_body_part(query):\n    query = query.lower()\n\n    # Exact match\n    exact = knowledge_base[knowledge_base['BodyPart'].str.lower() == query]\n    if not exact.empty:\n        return exact\n\n    # Synonym match\n    for part in knowledge_base['BodyPart']:\n        synonyms = get_synonyms(part.lower())\n        if query in synonyms:\n            return knowledge_base[knowledge_base['BodyPart'] == part]\n\n    # Fuzzy match\n    parts = knowledge_base['BodyPart'].str.lower().tolist()\n    close = get_close_matches(query, parts, n=1, cutoff=0.6)\n    if close:\n        return knowledge_base[knowledge_base['BodyPart'].str.lower() == close[0]]\n\n    return None\n\n# --- Example Interaction ---\nwhile True:\n    user_input = input(\"What's wrong? (type 'quit' to exit) \")\n    if user_input.lower() == 'quit':\n        break\n\n    result = find_body_part(user_input)\n    if result is not None:\n        for _, row in result.iterrows():\n            print(f\"â¡ Body Part: {row['BodyPart']}\")\n            print(f\"   Allegory: {row['Allegory']}\")\n            print(f\"   Bible Reference: {row['BibleReference']}\")\n    else:\n        print(\"âŒ No match found. Try another description.\")"}

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

Got it â€” letâ€™s add **MultiMatch support** so the app can recognize **multiple body parts in a single query** and return all the relevant verses/allegories at once.  

Hereâ€™s how the upgrade works:  

- It scans the query for **all possible matches** (exact, synonyms, fuzzy).  
- Instead of stopping at the first match, it collects **every match** it finds.  
- The response returns a list of **all body parts found**, each with their biblical notes.  

For example:  

**User input:**  
> "I saw something and then I took it."  

**App output:**  
- **Eye** â†’ "Matthew 6:22 â€” The eye is the lamp of the body."  
- **Hand** â†’ "Ecclesiastes 9:10 â€” Whatever your hand finds to do, do it with all your might."  

This way, it handles **compound actions**, which often tie multiple body parts into the allegory.  

ğŸ‘‰ Do you want me to update the **Python prototype code** now with this MultiMatch logic so you can test it?

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

{'content_type': 'code', 'language': 'unknown', 'response_format_name': None, 'text': 'import pandas as pd\r\nfrom rapidfuzz import fuzz\r\n\r\n# Load the CSV knowledge base (from earlier step)\r\nfile_path = \'/mnt/data/body_parts_knowledge_base.csv\'\r\nknowledge_base = pd.read_csv(file_path)\r\n\r\n# Create synonym dictionary for matching\r\nsynonyms = {\r\n    "eye": ["eyes", "sight", "see", "vision", "look"],\r\n    "hand": ["hands", "grasp", "take", "hold", "touch"],\r\n    "foot": ["feet", "walk", "step", "path", "legs"],\r\n    "heart": ["hearts", "love", "desire", "inner being"],\r\n    "head": ["heads", "mind", "thoughts", "thinking", "brain"],\r\n    "mouth": ["tongue", "speak", "words", "lips"],\r\n    "ear": ["ears", "listen", "hear", "hearing"],\r\n    "stomach": ["belly", "gut", "hunger", "appetite"],\r\n    "shoulder": ["shoulders", "burden", "carry"],\r\n}\r\n\r\ndef multimatch_query(user_input, threshold=80):\r\n    """\r\n    Finds all matching body parts in the user input using synonyms and fuzzy matching.\r\n    Returns a list of matches with biblical references and notes.\r\n    """\r\n    matches = []\r\n    user_input = user_input.lower()\r\n    \r\n    for idx, row in knowledge_base.iterrows():\r\n        body_part = row["BodyPart"].lower()\r\n        keywords = [body_part] + synonyms.get(body_part, [])\r\n        \r\n        for keyword in keywords:\r\n            score = fuzz.partial_ratio(keyword, user_input)\r\n            if score >= threshold:\r\n                matches.append({\r\n                    "BodyPart": row["BodyPart"],\r\n                    "Category": row["Category"],\r\n                    "BiblicalReference": row["BiblicalReference"],\r\n                    "Notes": row["Notes"],\r\n                    "MatchedKeyword": keyword\r\n                })\r\n                break  # stop after first synonym match for this body part\r\n    \r\n    return matches\r\n\r\n# Test the new multimatch with a compound query\r\ntest_query = "I saw something and then I took it."\r\nresults = multimatch_query(test_query)\r\n\r\nresults'}
---

{'content_type': 'code', 'language': 'unknown', 'response_format_name': None, 'text': 'import pandas as pd\r\nimport difflib\r\n\r\n# Load the updated CSV file\r\nfile_path = \'/mnt/data/body_knowledge_base.csv\'\r\nkb = pd.read_csv(file_path)\r\n\r\n# Simple lookup function with MultiMatch support\r\ndef lookup(query, top_n=3):\r\n    results = []\r\n    \r\n    # Direct keyword search (case insensitive)\r\n    mask = kb[\'Keywords\'].str.contains(query, case=False, na=False)\r\n    direct_matches = kb[mask]\r\n    if not direct_matches.empty:\r\n        for _, row in direct_matches.iterrows():\r\n            results.append({\r\n                "Part": row[\'BodyPart\'],\r\n                "Category": row[\'Category\'],\r\n                "Reference": row[\'BiblicalReference\'],\r\n                "Verse": row[\'VerseSummary\']\r\n            })\r\n    \r\n    # ### ğŸ”Š Updated TTS Script (auto-integrated with Spirit, Mind, Body layers)

```python
def generate_response(body_part, issue, kb):
    entry = kb.get(body_part, {})

    # Gather dimensions
    physical = entry.get("Physical Function", "")
    spiritual = entry.get("Spiritual Symbolism", "")
    mind = entry.get("Mind / Mental Reflection", "")
    scripture = entry.get("Scripture References", "")
    universal = entry.get("Universal Prescription", "")

    # Build truth-centered prescription
    response = f"""
You mentioned your {body_part} feels troubled.
Physically: {physical}.
Mentally: {mind}.
Spiritually: {spiritual}.

The truth is: {scripture}.
Even though the truth is hard, the real prescription is:
{universal}

Remember: healing may not always appear first in the body,
but it begins in the spirit, flows through the mind,
and becomes whole in the body â€” whole and whole, a miracle.
"""
    return response
```

### ğŸ“Œ Step 2: Local Script for TTS  
Below is a **Python script** you can run locally. It:  
1. Reads the CSV file.  
2. Generates speech audio for each entry.  
3. Saves each line as an `.mp3`.  
4. Packages them all into a single `.zip` file.  

```python
import pandas as pd
import pyttsx3
import os
import zipfile

# Load the CSV
df = pd.read_csv("universal_prescriptions.csv")

# Setup text-to-speech engine
engine = pyttsx3.init()
engine.setProperty("rate", 150)  # Adjust speaking speed
engine.setProperty("volume", 1.0)

# Output folder
output_folder = "tts_audio"
os.makedirs(output_folder, exist_ok=True)

# Generate audio files
for idx, row in df.iterrows():
    filename = f"{output_folder}/prescription_{row['ID']}.mp3"
    text = f"Condition: {row['Condition']}. Verse: {row['Verse']}. Prescription: {row['Prescription']}."
    engine.save_to_file(text, filename)

engine.runAndWait()

# Create ZIP package
zip_filename = "tts_prescriptions.zip"
with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_filename, 'w') as zipf:
    for file in os.listdir(output_folder):
        zipf.write(os.path.join(output_folder, file))

print(f"Done! All audio files saved in {zip_filename}")
```

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

Got it ğŸ‘ â€” hereâ€™s the updated script so that **both the MP3 files and the `prescriptions.csv` file** will be saved inside the `tts_audio/` folder.  

```python
import os
import csv
from gtts import gTTS

# Folder for saving everything
output_folder = "tts_audio"
os.makedirs(output_folder, exist_ok=True)

# List of prescriptions (each one will be its own MP3 and CSV entry)
prescriptions = [
    "The truth is, even though it is hard, the real prescription is forgiveness.",
    "The truth is, your healing might not be physical, but spiritual, in the heart, mind, or soul.",
    "The truth is, if you want to see physical miracles, begin in the spirit first, as in heaven, so on earth.",
    "The truth is, you already reached out for help, and that itself is a sign of faith.",
    "The truth is, you are not forsaken; it is we who forsake God. But He is near to the brokenhearted.",
    "The truth is, whole and whole, body and soul, a miracle."
]

# Save audio + build CSV
csv_path = os.path.join(output_folder, "prescriptions.csv")

with open(csv_path, mode="w", newline="", encoding="utf-8") as csvfile:
    writer = csv.writer(csvfile)
    writer.writerow(["File", "Prescription"])
    
    for i, line in enumerate(prescriptions, start=1):
        filename = f"prescription{i}.mp3"
        filepath = os.path.join(output_folder, filename)
        
        # Generate speech
        tts = gTTS(text=line, lang="en")
        tts.save(filepath)
        
        # Add row in CSV
        writer.writerow([filename, line])

print(f"âœ… All audio files and prescriptions.csv saved in: {os.path.abspath(output_folder)}")
```

When you run this script, youâ€™ll get:

```
/your-folder/
    generate_tts.py
    /tts_audio/
        prescription1.mp3
        prescription2.mp3
        prescription3.mp3
        prescription4.mp3
        prescription5.mp3
        prescription6.mp3
        prescriptions.csv
```

Each **MP3 matches a line in the CSV** so itâ€™s all mapped together.

```python
# generate_tts.py
import os
import csv
from gtts import gTTS

# Folder for saving everything
output_folder = "tts_audio"
os.makedirs(output_folder, exist_ok=True)

# List of prescriptions (each one will be its own MP3 and CSV entry)
prescriptions = [
    "The truth is, even though it is hard, the real prescription is forgiveness.",
    "The truth is, your healing might not be physical, but spiritual, in the heart, mind, or soul.",
    "The truth is, if you want to see physical miracles, begin in the spirit first, as in heaven, so on earth.",
    "The truth is, you already reached out for help, and that itself is a sign of faith.",
    "The truth is, you are not forsaken; it is we who forsake God. But He is near to the brokenhearted.",
    "The truth is, whole and whole, body and soul, a miracle."
]

# Save audio + build CSV
csv_path = os.path.join(output_folder, "prescriptions.csv")

with open(csv_path, mode="w", newline="", encoding="utf-8") as csvfile:
    writer = csv.writer(csvfile)
    writer.writerow(["File", "Prescription"])
    
    for i, line in enumerate(prescriptions, start=1):
        filename = f"prescription{i}.mp3"
        filepath = os.path.join(output_folder, filename)
        
        # Generate speech
        tts = gTTS(text=line, lang="en")
        tts.save(filepath)
        
        # Add row in CSV
        writer.writerow([filename, line])

print(f"âœ… All audio files and prescriptions.csv saved in: {os.path.abspath(output_folder)}")
```

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

Hereâ€™s the full code packaged cleanly:  

```python
# generate_tts.py
# This script generates text-to-speech audio files and a CSV package.

import os
import csv
from gtts import gTTS

# Prescriptions or universal truth-based lines
prescriptions = [
    "The truth is: the Lord is near to the brokenhearted and saves those crushed in spirit.",
    "Even though the truth is hard, the real prescription is: God gives and takes away, blessed be His name.",
    "The truth is: just by seeking help, you have already received help.",
    "The truth is: forgiveness is medicine. If you cannot heal it with love, forgiveness will have to do.",
    "The truth is: I came not only to heal your body, but also your soul. Altogether, whole and whole â€” a miracle.",
    "The truth is: healing begins in the spirit, then the mind, then the body. As in heaven, so on earth."
]

# Output folder
output_dir = "tts_audio"
os.makedirs(output_dir, exist_ok=True)

# CSV file path
csv_path = os.path.join(output_dir, "prescriptions.csv")

# Write CSV and generate audio files
with open(csv_path, mode="w", newline="", encoding="utf-8") as csvfile:
    writer = csv.writer(csvfile)
    writer.writerow(["Filename", "Text"])

    for idx, line in enumerate(prescriptions, start=1):
        filename = f"line_{idx}.mp3"
        filepath = os.path.join(output_dir, filename)

        # Generate audio
        tts = gTTS(text=line, lang="en")
        tts.save(filepath)

        # Write CSV row
        writer.writerow([filename, line])

print(f"âœ… All audio files and CSV have been generated in: {os.path.abspath(output_dir)}")
```

---

### ğŸ“Œ What this does:
1. Makes a folder called `tts_audio/`  
2. Saves **one `.mp3` file per line** (line_1.mp3, line_2.mp3, etc.)  
3. Creates a `prescriptions.csv` with filenames + text

## ğŸ—‚ Step 1: Converting CSV â†’ SQLite

Hereâ€™s a Python script that will:  
1. Read your current CSV.  
2. Create a SQLite database (`knowledge_base.db`).  
3. Store the body parts, categories, verses, prescriptions, and synonyms into a table.  

```python
import sqlite3
import pandas as pd

# Load CSV into pandas
csv_file = "knowledge_base.csv"   # <-- replace with your file path
df = pd.read_csv(csv_file)

# Connect to SQLite (creates if not exists)
conn = sqlite3.connect("knowledge_base.db")
cursor = conn.cursor()

# Create table
cursor.execute("""
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS knowledge (
    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
    body_part TEXT,
    category TEXT,
    verse TEXT,
    prescription TEXT,
    synonyms TEXT
)
""")

# Insert rows into the table
for _, row in df.iterrows():
    cursor.execute("""
    INSERT INTO knowledge (body_part, category, verse, prescription, synonyms)
    VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?)
    """, (
        row.get("Body Part", ""),
        row.get("Category", ""),
        row.get("Verse", ""),
        row.get("Prescription", ""),
        row.get("Synonyms", "")
    ))

# Commit & close
conn.commit()
conn.close()

print("âœ… knowledge_base.db created successfully!")
```

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

Perfect ğŸ‘Œ letâ€™s make the **query script** that will connect to your new `knowledge_base.db`, let you type in a keyword (like *â€œstomachâ€* or *â€œhungerâ€*), and return the **body part, category, verse, prescription, synonyms**.  

Hereâ€™s the script:  

```python
import sqlite3
import sys

def query_db(search_term):
    conn = sqlite3.connect("knowledge_base.db")
    cursor = conn.cursor()

    # Simple multi-match: search body_part, verse, prescription, synonyms
    cursor.execute("""
        SELECT body_part, category, verse, prescription, synonyms
        FROM knowledge
        WHERE body_part LIKE ?
        OR category LIKE ?
        OR verse LIKE ?
        OR prescription LIKE ?
        OR synonyms LIKE ?
    """, tuple([f"%{search_term}%"] * 5))

    results = cursor.fetchall()
    conn.close()
    return results

if __name__ == "__main__":
    if len(sys.argv) < 2:
        print("Usage: python query_db.py <search_term>")
    else:
        term = sys.argv[1]
        matches = query_db(term)
        if matches:
            for m in matches:
                print("ğŸ” Result:")
                print(f"  Body Part   : {m[0]}")
                print(f"  Category    : {m[1]}")
                print(f"  Verse       : {m[2]}")
                print(f"  Prescription: {m[3]}")
                print(f"  Synonyms    : {m[4]}")
                print("-" * 50)
        else:
            print("âŒ No matches found.")
```

### ğŸ«³ REFLECTING: Sharing From the Received Light

Got it ğŸ‘ weâ€™ll create a **new SQLite Knowledge Base file** (`knowledge_base.db`) from scratch. Iâ€™ll include a table schema so itâ€™s ready to hold **body parts, categories, verses, prescriptions, synonyms, and cross-links**.  

Hereâ€™s the script that will create it fresh:  

```python
import sqlite3

# Connect to a new SQLite DB (this will overwrite if already exists)
conn = sqlite3.connect("knowledge_base.db")
cursor = conn.cursor()

# Drop old table if it exists
cursor.execute("DROP TABLE IF EXISTS knowledge")

# Create fresh schema
cursor.execute("""
CREATE TABLE knowledge (
    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
    body_part TEXT NOT NULL,
    category TEXT,
    verse TEXT,
    prescription TEXT,
    synonyms TEXT,
    cross_links TEXT
)
""")

# Example seed data
data = [
    ("Heart", "Circulatory", 
     "Proverbs 4:23 - 'Above all else, guard your heart, for everything you do flows from it.'",
     "Keep your heart pure; meditate daily on Godâ€™s Word.",
     "core, spirit, soul, inner being",
     "Mind, Emotions"),

    ("Stomach", "Digestive",
     "John 6:35 - 'He who comes to Me shall never hunger.'",
     "Trust in Godâ€™s provision, spiritual fulfillment.",
     "belly, gut",
     "Mouth, Appetite"),

    ("Eye", "Sensory",
     "Matthew 6:22 - 'The eye is the lamp of the body.'",
     "Focus on what is pure and holy.",
     "vision, sight, gaze",
     "Mind, Hand"),

    ("Hand", "Action",
     "Ecclesiastes 9:10 - 'Whatever your hand finds to do, do it with all your might.'",
     "Do good works with diligence and integrity.",
     "palm, grip",
     "Eye, Mind")
]

cursor.executemany("""
INSERT INTO knowledge (body_part, category, verse, prescription, synonyms, cross_links)
VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?, ?)
""", data)

conn.commit()
conn.close()

print("âœ… New knowledge_base.db created successfully with seed data.")
```

---

### ğŸ”§ How to use it
1. Save this file as `create_db.py`.  
2. Run it:  

```bash
python create_db.py
```

3. It will generate a **new `knowledge_base.db`** with the structure + example seed data.
